; Allwinner H3 chip bootrom
; 32K from address 0xffff0000

; Note how this disassembly byte swaps.
; odx gives the true byte order:
;  0800 00ea 0600 00ea 0500 00ea 0400 00ea
; This disassembler fetches (as does the processor)
; 32 bit items, then byte swaps them for display
; (as the processor does for execution).
; This is fine for opcodes, but does not do well for strings.
; However, there are almost no strings in this binary.
;
; In fact, just these (from the odx dump):
;  ffff2c00 0700 00ea 0700 00ea 6547 4f4e 2e42 524d           eGON.BRM
;  ffff3000 6547 4f4e 2e42 5430 0000 0000 0020 a0e1   eGON.BT0        
;  ffff4bd0 f7ff ffea 6547 4f4e 2e42 5430 0000 0000       eGON.BT0    
;  ffff50d0 6547 4f4e 2e42 5430 0000 0000 0100 a0e3   eGON.BT0        
;  ffff7790 0000 e0e3 f7ff ffea 6547 4f4e 2e42 5430           eGON.BT0

; This is how a new core starts running.
; The kernel places an address in PRIVATE0 (0x01f01da4)
; Reset brings the new core into the ROM and we
;  branch to the specified
;- ffff2e0c:       01f01da4        ; holds address we jump to .. PRIVATE0
;- ffff2e10:       01f01dac        ; if the contents of this (PRIVATE1) match ..
;- ffff2e14:       fa50392f        ; this magic number

ffff2c3c:	e59f01c8 	ldr	r0, [pc, #456]	; 0xffff2e0c (PRIVATE0)
ffff2c40:	e590f000 	ldr	pc, [r0]

; normal startup path comes here.
; reads processor affinity register (holds core number in low 2 bits)

ffff2c50:	1afffff9 	bne	0xffff2c3c

; check for non zero cluster number (unlikely)

ffff2c5c:	1afffff6 	bne	0xffff2c3c
